Chris, glad you got to have your FU moment regarding the BS lawsuit.   That being said,  it is without question that Carroll Shelby is a legend, he was also every bit as litigious as Helicki is.  I raced vintage Shelbys for many years and had many interactions with him before his passing.  In his later years he was very well known for suing many, many people,  even including the national club dedicated to his cars.  To this day  I have a bumpersticker on my tool box that was common in this timeframe with Shelby owners that said "Honk if you are being sued by Carroll".  Many of us that are dedicated to the Shelby cars, especially the vintage ones paid homage to the history, loved the cars, paid tribute to the legend, but held our noses and tongues regarding the character of the man.  I don't say all of this to temper your enthusiasm for the car or the desire to build one, just to let you know that the man, Shelby, was the same type of person as the one that sued you.  I laughed while watching your video because in my perception, two parties of similar tendencies decided to duke it out.  If you are curious if what I say is true, just google Carroll Shelby lawsuits and enjoy the ride. Despite all of the above diatribe, love the channel and your journey from the beginning of learning how to work on cars.  I will be watching whatever your various projects, even if it is a Shelby "not an Eleanor" tribute.

You obviously have way more info on this than me. However, I believe at the time they copyrighted the "Character" muscle car (intentional vagueness), it was to gain royalties from companies that made toy models like Revell. It was attempt to get as many royalties in areas that were being lost to other companies, brands, and franchises. Eventually those extra charges are what caused a lot of model building companies to die out. Entertainment movies are expensive and royalties from sales in every genre possible from a Happy Meal to a sticker set of magnets is how they recoup their losses and make profits. It sounds like their is one hell of a strong legal group that is trying to do that, but may have over reached. Sorry for your troubles.

Great video but you missed out some information. The Eleanor Mustang is a 1971 Mustang Mach used in HB Halickis Gone in 60 seconds and was featured in Junk Yard Man as well. HB Halicki the Car Crash King was tragically killed whilst filming Gone in 60 seconds 2/3. In your case, Halicki was being childish and did not want anyone creating their version of "Eleanor," unless Halicki was making profit.  You can create a lawsuit for damages, the cost of the vehicle, as if the car was completed, attorney fees, and "inter Alia." The "Eleanor" isn't even a GT500. I personally think the Eleanor Mustang is ugly as sin (including the side-pipes, hood bulge, and the stupid relocation of the running lights into the headlight bucket). I cringe whenever I see a picture of one.  The center-grill lights were only used on the early 67 Shelby's. California had laws at the time regarding the distance between headlights, so Shelby relocated them to the outside corners. The front valance is indeed inspired by the 1965 R-Model GT350, and was done to improve cooling. I think there is a game people play when you say "In my opinion"...
You're missing one main point. In the Nick Cage "Gone in 60 Seconds" Eleanor represents ANY 67 Shelby GT 500. It's not just one that has a few mods and is painted grey. If you remember from the movie all the cars have names. Before they have seen any of the cars they are going to steal, they give them names. Now the names are more nefarious because it's a code for cars they want to steal but the fact remains, the crew sees 67 Shelby GT 500 on the list and they immediately say Eleanor and refer to that car as Raines' unicorn, which he refers to it again when it's being crushed. At the end of the movie Kip buys him Eleanor which is a rusted out in need of restoration 67 Shelby GT 500. Not painted grey no additional mods but a stock looking 67 Shelby GT 500. At best, because the grey restomod (what I'm calling it) was the star of the movie, they might be able to make a claim on that particular design and paint color but nothing more. Here is the kicker. As you pointed out there are some mods on the movie car that make it NOT a Shelby so maybe it's a Shelby clone or maybe someone killed the value and modded it. Back to my point, Shelbys are numbered chassis. If the car in the movie is in fact a Shelby GT 500 then it's already copyrighted. If it's a 67 Mustang made to look like a modded Shelby then again the only claim is to those specific mods and the paint color because they sure as hell can't copyright a Mustang. I realize all of this is moot point but I just wanted to mention that I'm glad a court told them that you can't stand on the shoulders of icons, give it a paint job and fog lights and say you own the design.
